<p><b>Fußballclub Gelsenkirchen-Schalke 04 e. V.</b>, commonly known as <b>FC Schalke 04</b> (<small>German:</small> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_German" title="Help:IPA for German">[ʔɛf t͡seː ˈʃalkə nʊl fiːɐ̯]</a></span>) or simply abbreviated as <b>S04</b> (<small>German:</small> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_German" title="Help:IPA for German">[ˈʔɛs nʊl fiːɐ̯]</a></span>), is a <a href="/wiki/Professionalism_in_association_football" title="Professionalism in association football">professional</a> <a href="/wiki/Football_in_Germany" title="Football in Germany">German association-football club</a> and multi-<a href="/wiki/Sports_club" title="Sports club">sports club</a> originally from the <a class="extiw" href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gelsenkirchen-Schalke" title="de:Gelsenkirchen-Schalke">Schalke</a> district of <a href="/wiki/Gelsenkirchen" title="Gelsenkirchen">Gelsenkirchen</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Rhine-Westphalia" title="North Rhine-Westphalia">North Rhine-Westphalia</a>. The "04" in the club's name derives from its formation in 1904. Schalke has long been one of the most popular professional <a href="/wiki/Football_team" title="Football team">football teams</a> and multi-sports club in Germany, even though major successes have been rare since the club's heyday in the 1930s and early 1940s. Schalke play in the <a href="/wiki/Bundesliga" title="Bundesliga">Bundesliga</a>, the top tier of the <a href="/wiki/German_football_league_system" title="German football league system">German football league system</a>. As of December 2015, the club has 140,000 members, making it the second-largest sports club in Germany and the sixth-largest sports club in the world in terms of membership.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> Other activities offered by the club include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Athletics_(track_and_field)" title="Athletics (track and field)">athletics (track and field)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Team_handball" title="Team handball">handball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Table_tennis" title="Table tennis">table tennis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Winter_sport" title="Winter sport">winter sports</a>, and <a href="/wiki/ESports" title="ESports">eSports</a>.</p>
<p>Founded in 1904, Schalke has won seven <a href="/wiki/List_of_German_football_champions" title="List of German football champions">German championships</a>, five <a href="/wiki/DFB-Pokal" title="DFB-Pokal">DFB-Pokals</a>, one <a href="/wiki/DFL-Supercup" title="DFL-Supercup">DFL-Supercup</a> and one <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Europa_League" title="UEFA Europa League">UEFA Cup</a>.</p>
<p>Since 2001, Schalke's stadium is the <a href="/wiki/Veltins-Arena" title="Veltins-Arena">Veltins-Arena</a>. Schalke holds a long-standing rivalry with <a href="/wiki/Ruhr" title="Ruhr">Ruhr</a> neighbours <a href="/wiki/Borussia_Dortmund" title="Borussia Dortmund">Borussia Dortmund</a>, arguably one of the most widespread and well-known rivalries in German football, and matches between the two teams are referred to as the <a href="/wiki/Revierderby" title="Revierderby">Revierderby</a>.</p>
<p>Schalke was ranked as the seventh-best football team in Europe by <a href="/wiki/UEFA" title="UEFA">UEFA</a>'s 2015 <a href="/wiki/UEFA_coefficient#Club_coefficient" title="UEFA coefficient">UEFA club rankings</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UEFA_Team_Ranking_2015_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-UEFA_Team_Ranking_2015-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>In terms of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Operating_income" title="Operating income">operating income</a>, Schalke possesses the seventh-highest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Operating_income" title="Operating income">operating income</a> of any football club at "<a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">$</a>64.4 million or <a href="/wiki/Pound_sterling" title="Pound sterling">£</a>38.2 million (<a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">€</a>48 million)",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Forbes_List_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-Forbes_List-6">[6]</a></sup> and 0% <a href="/wiki/Debt" title="Debt">debt</a> as of August 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Schalke_04_-_Forbes_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-Schalke_04_-_Forbes-7">[7]</a></sup> Schalke also generates the 14th-highest <a href="/wiki/Revenue" title="Revenue">revenue</a> of any football club, at "$265.6 million or £157.8 million (€198 million)".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Schalke_04_-_Forbes_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-Schalke_04_-_Forbes-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>In May 2014, Schalke 04 were ranked by <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> magazine as the <a href="/wiki/Forbes%27_list_of_the_most_valuable_football_clubs" title="Forbes' list of the most valuable football clubs">14th-most valuable football club</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Forbes_List_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-Forbes_List-6">[6]</a></sup> at "£355.3 million or $598.5 million (€446 million)", an increase of 16% from the previous year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Schalke_04_-_Forbes_7-2"><a href="#cite_note-Schalke_04_-_Forbes-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Schalke_04&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Schalke.27s_early_years">Schalke's early years</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Schalke_04&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Schalke's early years">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:257px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F015017-0006,_Gelsenkirchen-Buer,_Kohlebergbau.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="585" data-file-width="800" height="186" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F015017-0006%2C_Gelsenkirchen-Buer%2C_Kohlebergbau.jpg/255px-Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F015017-0006%2C_Gelsenkirchen-Buer%2C_Kohlebergbau.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F015017-0006%2C_Gelsenkirchen-Buer%2C_Kohlebergbau.jpg/383px-Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F015017-0006%2C_Gelsenkirchen-Buer%2C_Kohlebergbau.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F015017-0006%2C_Gelsenkirchen-Buer%2C_Kohlebergbau.jpg/510px-Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F015017-0006%2C_Gelsenkirchen-Buer%2C_Kohlebergbau.jpg 2x" width="255"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F015017-0006,_Gelsenkirchen-Buer,_Kohlebergbau.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
1900s typical mining structure in the Ruhr, source of the Schalke nickname Die Knappen – from an old German word for "miners"– because the team drew so many of its players and supporters from the coalmine workers of Gelsenkirchen.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The club was founded on 4 May 1904 as <b>Westfalia Schalke</b> by a group of high school students and first wore the colours red and yellow. The team was unable to gain admittance to the <i>Westdeutscher Spielverband</i> and played in one of the "wild associations" of early German football. In 1912, after years of failed attempts to join the official league, they merged with the gymnastic club <b>Schalker Turnverein 1877</b> in order to facilitate their entry. This arrangement held up until 1915 when <b>SV Westfalia Schalke</b> was re-established as an independent club. The separation proved short-lived and the two came together again in 1919 as <b>Turn- und Sportverein Schalke 1877</b>. The new club won its first honours in 1923 as champions of the <i>Schalke Kreisliga</i>. It was around this time that Schalke picked up the nickname <i>Die Knappen</i> – from an old German word for "miners" because the team drew so many of its players and supporters from the coalmine workers of Gelsenkirchen.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In 1924, the football team parted ways with the gymnasts again, this time taking the club chairman along with them. They took the name <b>FC Schalke 04</b> and adopted the now familiar blue and white <a href="/wiki/Kit_(association_football)" title="Kit (association football)">kit</a> from which their second nickname would derive – <i>Die Königsblauen</i> (English: The Royal Blues). The following year, the club became the dominant local side, based on a style of play that used short, sharp, man-to-man passing to move the ball. This system would later become famous as the <i>Schalker Kreisel</i> (English: spinning top; gyroscope). In 1927, it carried them into the top-flight <i>Gauliga Ruhr</i>, onto the league championship, and then into the opening rounds of the national finals.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rise_to_dominance">Rise to dominance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Schalke_04&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Rise to dominance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:257px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Schalke_DFBpokal_schief2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1569" data-file-width="1000" height="400" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Schalke_DFBpokal_schief2.jpg/255px-Schalke_DFBpokal_schief2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Schalke_DFBpokal_schief2.jpg/383px-Schalke_DFBpokal_schief2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Schalke_DFBpokal_schief2.jpg/510px-Schalke_DFBpokal_schief2.jpg 2x" width="255"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Schalke_DFBpokal_schief2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
S04 won the <a href="/wiki/DFB-Pokal" title="DFB-Pokal">DFB-Pokal</a> for the first time in its history in the <a href="/wiki/1937_Tschammerpokal" title="1937 Tschammerpokal">1937 Tschammerpokal</a>. The DFB-Pokal of Schalke 04, the successor to the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tschammerpokal#Tschammer-Pokal" title="Tschammerpokal">Tschammerpokal</a></i> displayed at the S04 <a href="/wiki/Museum" title="Museum">museum</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The popular club built a new stadium, the Glückauf-Kampfbahn, in 1928, and acknowledged the city's support by renaming themselves <b>FC Gelsenkirchen-Schalke 04</b>. They won their first West German championship in 1929, but the following year were sanctioned for exceeding salary levels set by the league and, in an era that considered professionalism in sport to be anathema, found themselves banned from play for nearly half a year.</p>
<p>However, the ban had little impact on the team's popularity: in their first game after the ban against <a href="/wiki/Fortuna_D%C3%BCsseldorf" title="Fortuna Düsseldorf">Fortuna Düsseldorf</a>, in June 1931, the team drew 70,000 to its home ground. The club's fortunes begun to rise from 1931 and they made a semi-final appearance in the <a href="/wiki/1932_German_football_championship" title="1932 German football championship">1932 German championship</a>, losing 1–2 to <a href="/wiki/Eintracht_Frankfurt" title="Eintracht Frankfurt">Eintracht Frankfurt</a>. <a href="/wiki/1933_German_football_championship" title="1933 German football championship">The year after</a>, the club went all the way to the final, where Fortuna Düsseldorf proved the better side, winning 3–0.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>With the re-organisation of German football in 1933 under <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a>, Schalke found themselves in the <a href="/wiki/Gauliga_Westfalen" title="Gauliga Westfalen">Gauliga Westfalen</a>, one of sixteen top-flight divisions established to replace the innumerable regional and local leagues, all claiming top status. This league saw Schalke's most successful decade in their history: from 1933 to 1942, the club would appear in 14 of 18 national finals (ten in the German championship and eight in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tschammerpokal#Tschammer-Pokal" title="Tschammerpokal">Tschammerpokal</a>, the predecessor of today's <a href="/wiki/DFB-Pokal" title="DFB-Pokal">DFB-Pokal</a>) and win their league in every one of its eleven seasons.</p>
<p>The club never lost a home game in the Gauliga Westfalen in all these eleven seasons and only lost six away games, while remaining entirely unbeaten in the seasons 1935–36, 1936–37, 1937–38, 1938–39, 1940–41 and 1942–43, a sign of the club's dominance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_championship_years_1934.E2.80.9342">The championship years 1934–42</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Schalke_04&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: The championship years 1934–42">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-2004-1001-503,_Berlin,_Zuschauer_beim_Fu%C3%9Fball-Endspiel.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="547" data-file-width="800" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-2004-1001-503%2C_Berlin%2C_Zuschauer_beim_Fu%C3%9Fball-Endspiel.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-2004-1001-503%2C_Berlin%2C_Zuschauer_beim_Fu%C3%9Fball-Endspiel.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-2004-1001-503%2C_Berlin%2C_Zuschauer_beim_Fu%C3%9Fball-Endspiel.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-2004-1001-503%2C_Berlin%2C_Zuschauer_beim_Fu%C3%9Fball-Endspiel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-2004-1001-503%2C_Berlin%2C_Zuschauer_beim_Fu%C3%9Fball-Endspiel.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-2004-1001-503%2C_Berlin%2C_Zuschauer_beim_Fu%C3%9Fball-Endspiel.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-2004-1001-503,_Berlin,_Zuschauer_beim_Fu%C3%9Fball-Endspiel.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
FC Schalke 04 supporters in 1941</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Schalke's first <a href="/wiki/List_of_German_football_champions#German_football_championships_under_the_Third_Reich_.281933.E2.80.9345.29" title="List of German football champions">national title</a> came in <a href="/wiki/1934_German_football_championship" title="1934 German football championship">1934</a> with a 2–1 victory over favourites <a href="/wiki/1._FC_N%C3%BCrnberg" title="1. FC Nürnberg">1. FC Nürnberg</a>. <a href="/wiki/1935_German_football_championship" title="1935 German football championship">The next year</a>, they successfully defended their title against <a href="/wiki/VfB_Stuttgart" title="VfB Stuttgart">VfB Stuttgart</a> with a 6–4 win. The club missed the <a href="/wiki/1936_German_football_championship" title="1936 German football championship">1936</a> final, but would make appearances in the championship match in each of the next six years, coming away victorious in <a href="/wiki/1937_German_football_championship" title="1937 German football championship">1937</a>, <a href="/wiki/1939_German_football_championship" title="1939 German football championship">1939</a>, <a href="/wiki/1940_German_football_championship" title="1940 German football championship">1940</a> and <a href="/wiki/1942_German_football_championship" title="1942 German football championship">1942</a>. Three of those national finals were against Austrian teams –<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/VfB_Admira_Wacker_M%C3%B6dling" title="VfB Admira Wacker Mödling">Admira Wien</a>, <a href="/wiki/SK_Rapid_Wien" title="SK Rapid Wien">Rapid Wien</a>, and <a href="/wiki/First_Vienna_FC" title="First Vienna FC">First Vienna</a>– which played in Germany's Gauliga Ostmark after Austria's incorporation into the Reich through the 1938 <i><a href="/wiki/Anschluss" title="Anschluss">Anschluss</a></i>.</p>
<p><i>Die Königsblauen</i> also made frequent appearances in the final of the Tschammerpokal, but enjoyed much less success there. They lost the <a href="/wiki/1935_Tschammerpokal" title="1935 Tschammerpokal">inaugural Tschammerpokal</a> 0–2 to 1. FC Nürnberg in 1935. They also made failed appearances in the <a href="/wiki/1936_Tschammerpokal" title="1936 Tschammerpokal">1936</a>, <a href="/wiki/1941_Tschammerpokal" title="1941 Tschammerpokal">1941</a>, and <a href="/wiki/1942_Tschammerpokal" title="1942 Tschammerpokal">1942</a> finals with their only victory coming in <a href="/wiki/1937_Tschammerpokal" title="1937 Tschammerpokal">1937</a> against Fortuna Düsseldorf.</p>
<p>Over a dozen seasons, from 1933 to 1945, Schalke won 162 of 189 Gauliga matches, drawing 21 and losing only 6. On the way, they scored 924 goals and gave up just 145. From 1935 to 1939, they did not lose a single league match. The club's dominance throughout this period led them to be held up for propaganda purposes by the <a href="/wiki/Nazism" title="Nazism">Nazi</a> regime, as an example of "new Germany".</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-war_football">Post-war football</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Schalke_04&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Post-war football">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:257px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kuzorra87.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1199" data-file-width="811" height="377" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Kuzorra87.jpg/255px-Kuzorra87.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Kuzorra87.jpg/383px-Kuzorra87.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Kuzorra87.jpg/510px-Kuzorra87.jpg 2x" width="255"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kuzorra87.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Commonly regarded as the greatest S04 player of all time <a href="/wiki/Ernst_Kuzorra" title="Ernst Kuzorra">Ernst Kuzorra</a> alongside <a href="/wiki/Fritz_Szepan" title="Fritz Szepan">Fritz Szepan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ernst_Kuzorra" title="Ernst Kuzorra">Ernst Kuzorra</a> is also commonly regarded as one of the greatest German <a href="/wiki/Forward_(association_football)" title="Forward (association football)">forwards</a> and led S04 to become the dominant team in <a href="/wiki/Football_in_Germany" title="Football in Germany">German football</a> winning six <a href="/wiki/List_of_German_football_champions" title="List of German football champions">German championships</a> and one <a href="/wiki/DFB-Pokal" title="DFB-Pokal">DFB-Pokal</a> from 1934 to 1942. <a href="/wiki/Ernst_Kuzorra" title="Ernst Kuzorra">Ernst Kuzorra</a> was one of the main axes of what became known as the "<b>Schalker Kreisel</b>; a system that used quick and short <a href="/wiki/Passing_(association_football)" title="Passing (association football)">passing</a>", to confuse and overwhelm the opponent.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>With Germany in chaos towards the end of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, Schalke played just two matches in 1945. They resumed regular play following the war and, for a time, continued to compete as a strong side. They set a record in a national championship round match with a 20–0 drubbing of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2nd_Oberliga_West#Overview" title="2nd Oberliga West">SpVgg Herten</a>, but that spoke more to the weakened condition of German football than the ability of the team. Schalke's play fell off and the best they could manage in the new Oberliga West in 1947 was a sixth-place finish; within two years, they slipped to 12th place.</p>
<p>It would take Schalke until the mid-1950s to recover their form. They finished third in a tight three-way race for the 1954 Oberliga West title, decided on the last day of the season. The following year, they appeared in the <a href="/wiki/1954%E2%80%9355_DFB-Pokal" title="1954–55 DFB-Pokal">DFB-Pokal</a> final, where they lost 2–3 to <a href="/wiki/Karlsruher_SC" title="Karlsruher SC">Karlsruher SC</a>. The club's next, and to date last, German championship came in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_football_championship_1958" title="German football championship 1958">1958</a> with a 3–0 victory over <a href="/wiki/Hamburger_SV" title="Hamburger SV">Hamburger SV</a>. The strong fanbase of the club is as well documented in a local church, St. Joseph, in Gelsenkirchen. It was renovated shortly after the 1958 victory, where one of the glass windows shows <a href="/wiki/Aloysius_Gonzaga" title="Aloysius Gonzaga">Aloysius Gonzaga</a> with a football and the dress and colors of Schalke.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Entry_to_the_Bundesliga">Entry to the Bundesliga</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Schalke_04&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Entry to the Bundesliga">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Schalke continued to play well, delivering a number of top four finishes in the years leading up to the 1963 formation of the <a href="/wiki/Bundesliga" title="Bundesliga">Bundesliga</a>, West Germany's new federal, professional league. Those results earned them selection as one of sixteen sides admitted to the top-flight league.</p>
<p>Their first years in the Bundesliga were difficult. In <a href="/wiki/1964%E2%80%9365_Bundesliga" title="1964–65 Bundesliga">1964–65</a>, they escaped relegation only through the expansion of the league to 18 teams. A number of finishes at the lower end of the league table followed, before a marked improvement in <a href="/wiki/1971%E2%80%9372_Bundesliga" title="1971–72 Bundesliga">1971–72</a>, culminating in a second-place finish to <a href="/wiki/FC_Bayern_Munich" title="FC Bayern Munich">Bayern Munich</a> and after having led the league for much of the season. In the same season, Schalke won the <a href="/wiki/1971%E2%80%9372_DFB-Pokal" title="1971–72 DFB-Pokal">DFB-Pokal</a> for the second time in its history.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Bundesliga_scandal_of_1971">The Bundesliga scandal of 1971</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Schalke_04&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: The Bundesliga scandal of 1971">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Despite their improved results, the seeds of a major reversal had already been sown. A number of the team's players and officials were accused of accepting <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bribes#Sport_corruption" title="Bribes">bribes</a> as part of the widespread <a href="/wiki/Bundesliga_scandal_(1971)" title="Bundesliga scandal (1971)">Bundesliga scandal of 1971</a>. Investigation showed that Schalke had deliberately played to lose their 17 May, 28th-round match against <a href="/wiki/Arminia_Bielefeld" title="Arminia Bielefeld">Arminia Bielefeld</a> by a score of 0–1. As a result, several Schalke players were banned for life, including three —<a href="/wiki/Klaus_Fischer" title="Klaus Fischer">Klaus Fischer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Reinhard_Libuda" title="Reinhard Libuda">"Stan" Libuda</a> and <a href="/wiki/Klaus_Fichtel" title="Klaus Fichtel">Klaus Fichtel</a>— who regularly played for the <a href="/wiki/Germany_national_football_team" title="Germany national football team">German national team</a> at the time.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Even though the penalties were later commuted to bans ranging from six months to two years, the scandal had a profound effect on what might have possibly become one of the dominant German teams of the 1970s.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Crisis_and_recovery">Crisis and recovery</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Schalke_04&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Crisis and recovery">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:257px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Internazionale-Schalke_04_1997-05-21.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="738" data-file-width="534" height="352" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Internazionale-Schalke_04_1997-05-21.svg/255px-Internazionale-Schalke_04_1997-05-21.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Internazionale-Schalke_04_1997-05-21.svg/383px-Internazionale-Schalke_04_1997-05-21.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Internazionale-Schalke_04_1997-05-21.svg/510px-Internazionale-Schalke_04_1997-05-21.svg.png 2x" width="255"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Internazionale-Schalke_04_1997-05-21.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
FC Schalke 04 starting line-up in their victorious <a href="/wiki/1997_UEFA_Cup_Final" title="1997 UEFA Cup Final">1997 UEFA Cup Final</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1973, the club moved to the <a href="/wiki/Parkstadion" title="Parkstadion">Parkstadion</a>, newly built for the <a href="/wiki/1974_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1974 FIFA World Cup">1974 FIFA World Cup</a> and having a capacity of 70,000 spectators. In the wake of the scandal, the club's performance was uneven. They managed another second-place result in <a href="/wiki/1976%E2%80%9377_Bundesliga" title="1976–77 Bundesliga">1976–77</a>, finishing just one point behind champions <a href="/wiki/Borussia_M%C3%B6nchengladbach" title="Borussia Mönchengladbach">Borussia Mönchengladbach</a>.</p>
<p>In the early 1980s, <i>Die Knappen</i> ran into trouble and found themselves relegated to the <a href="/wiki/2._Bundesliga" title="2. Bundesliga">second division of the Bundesliga</a> for the 1981–82 season and, after promotion, again in 1983–84. They returned to the top flight in <a href="/wiki/1984%E2%80%9385_Bundesliga" title="1984–85 Bundesliga">1984</a> but slipped once more to the second tier in 1988. They returned to the Bundesliga in the <a href="/wiki/1991%E2%80%9392_Bundesliga" title="1991–92 Bundesliga">1991–92</a> season and have stayed in the top flight ever since.</p>
<p>The club earned their first honours since the DFB-Pokal win of <a href="/wiki/1971%E2%80%9372_DFB-Pokal" title="1971–72 DFB-Pokal">1972</a> with a victory in the final of the <a href="/wiki/1996%E2%80%9397_UEFA_Cup" title="1996–97 UEFA Cup">1996–97 UEFA Cup</a> over <a href="/wiki/Inter_Milan" title="Inter Milan">Inter Milan</a> on penalties. Coached by the Dutch coach <a href="/wiki/Huub_Stevens" title="Huub Stevens">Huub Stevens</a>, the 1997 Schalke squad earned the nickname "Euro Fighters", which is still in use among fans. Stevens, who was widely unknown in Germany at the time, quickly earned himself a cult following among the Schalke supporters.</p>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright" style="background-color:#0070FF">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:419px;max-width:419px;background-color:#0070FF">
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;background-color:#0070FF;margin:1px;width:133px;max-width:133px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Schalke_Asamoah_06.jpg"><img alt="Gerald Asamoah with Schalke 04" data-file-height="218" data-file-width="153" height="187" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Schalke_Asamoah_06.jpg/131px-Schalke_Asamoah_06.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/21/Schalke_Asamoah_06.jpg 1.5x" width="131"/></a></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;background-color:#0070FF;margin:1px;width:282px;max-width:282px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Schalker_Pokaljubel01.jpg"><img alt="Schalker Schalke 04 celebrate winning the DFB-Pokal" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="1536" height="187" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Schalker_Pokaljubel01.jpg/280px-Schalker_Pokaljubel01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Schalker_Pokaljubel01.jpg/420px-Schalker_Pokaljubel01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Schalker_Pokaljubel01.jpg/560px-Schalker_Pokaljubel01.jpg 2x" width="280"/></a></div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center;background-color:#FFFFFF"><span style="color:#0070FF"><a href="/wiki/Gerald_Asamoah" title="Gerald Asamoah">Gerald Asamoah</a> was the S04 leading goal-scoring figure from the turn of the 21st century through to the mid 2000s as well as playing over 250 games for S04 over 11 years and Schalke players celebrate winning the <a href="/wiki/DFB-Pokal" title="DFB-Pokal">DFB-Pokal</a> in <a href="/wiki/2001%E2%80%9302_DFB-Pokal" title="2001–02 DFB-Pokal">2002</a></span></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Stevens successfully implemented a system of rigid discipline, especially in the defence. His motto "<i>Die Null muß stehen</i>" (in <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a>, "It has to read nil"), which emphasized his importance on his side not conceding any goals, has found its way into everyday language in Germany.</p>
<p>The turn of the millennium has seen much stronger performances from Schalke. During the 1990s and early 2000, the club underwent a successful transformation into a modern, commercial sports organisation and established itself as one of the dominant teams of the Bundesliga. Schalke captured consecutive DFB-Pokals in <a href="/wiki/2000%E2%80%9301_DFB-Pokal" title="2000–01 DFB-Pokal">2000–01</a> and <a href="/wiki/2001%E2%80%9302_DFB-Pokal" title="2001–02 DFB-Pokal">2001–02</a>, and earned second-place finishes in the Bundesliga in <a href="/wiki/2000%E2%80%9301_Bundesliga" title="2000–01 Bundesliga">2000–01</a>, <a href="/wiki/2004%E2%80%9305_Bundesliga" title="2004–05 Bundesliga">2004–05</a> and <a href="/wiki/2006%E2%80%9307_Bundesliga" title="2006–07 Bundesliga">2006–07</a>. The <a href="/wiki/2000%E2%80%9301_FC_Schalke_04_season" title="2000–01 FC Schalke 04 season">2000–01</a> season finish was heartbreaking for Schalke's supporters as it took a goal in the fourth minute of injury time by Bayern Munich away to Hamburger SV to snatch the title from <i>Die Königsblauen</i>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Current">Current</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Schalke_04&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Current">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_FC_Schalke_04_season" title="2013–14 FC Schalke 04 season">2013–14 FC Schalke 04 season</a> and <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_FC_Schalke_04_season" title="2014–15 FC Schalke 04 season">2014–15 FC Schalke 04 season</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Schalke_04_Fans_664.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1900" data-file-width="2500" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Schalke_04_Fans_664.jpg/220px-Schalke_04_Fans_664.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Schalke_04_Fans_664.jpg/330px-Schalke_04_Fans_664.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Schalke_04_Fans_664.jpg/440px-Schalke_04_Fans_664.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Schalke_04_Fans_664.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Fans displaying their colours at the <a href="/wiki/Veltins-Arena" title="Veltins-Arena">Veltins-Arena</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The last few years have been more successful for Schalke, who finished in the second place in 2005, a result that led to Schalke making its second appearance in the <a href="/wiki/2005%E2%80%9306_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2005–06 UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a>. There, Schalke finished in third place during the group stage and continuing into the <a href="/wiki/2005%E2%80%9306_UEFA_Cup" title="2005–06 UEFA Cup">UEFA Cup</a>, where they were eliminated by the eventual winners <a href="/wiki/Sevilla_FC" title="Sevilla FC">Sevilla</a> in the semi-finals. In <a href="/wiki/2005%E2%80%9306_Bundesliga" title="2005–06 Bundesliga">2005–06</a>, Schalke finished in fourth place in the Bundesliga and a year later they again finished as runners-up for the third time in seven seasons.</p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2007–08 UEFA Champions League">2007–08 season</a>, Schalke progressed past the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">Champions League</a> group stage for the first time and advanced to the quarter-finals after beating <a href="/wiki/FC_Porto" title="FC Porto">Porto</a> on penalties in the round of 16. They were stopped by <a href="/wiki/FC_Barcelona" title="FC Barcelona">Barcelona</a> in the quarter-finals, losing both home and away games 0–1.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:VeltinsArena_at_friendly_Schalke_04_-_Zenit_St._Petersburg.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2112" data-file-width="2816" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/VeltinsArena_at_friendly_Schalke_04_-_Zenit_St._Petersburg.JPG/220px-VeltinsArena_at_friendly_Schalke_04_-_Zenit_St._Petersburg.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/VeltinsArena_at_friendly_Schalke_04_-_Zenit_St._Petersburg.JPG/330px-VeltinsArena_at_friendly_Schalke_04_-_Zenit_St._Petersburg.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/VeltinsArena_at_friendly_Schalke_04_-_Zenit_St._Petersburg.JPG/440px-VeltinsArena_at_friendly_Schalke_04_-_Zenit_St._Petersburg.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:VeltinsArena_at_friendly_Schalke_04_-_Zenit_St._Petersburg.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Schalke 04 <a href="/wiki/Royal_blue" title="Royal blue">royal blue</a> trademark <a href="/wiki/Jersey_(clothing)" title="Jersey (clothing)">jersey</a> with sponsor Gazprom elaborately showcased prior to a match with Zenit Saint Petersburg at the Veltins-Arena to celebrate Gazprom's investment of over €125 million in S04.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 9 October 2006, Russian oil company <a href="/wiki/Gazprom" title="Gazprom">Gazprom</a> became the club's new sponsor. The company stated it expects to invest as much as €125 million in the club over a five-and-a-half year period.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> Gazprom's sponsorship has been seen by some analysts as a politically motivated attempt to buy friendship in Germany.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> Within this sponsorship, Schalke 04 and <a href="/wiki/FC_Zenit_Saint_Petersburg" title="FC Zenit Saint Petersburg">Zenit Saint Petersburg</a> signed a "partnership agreement". Both clubs intend to work closely on improving football-related issues.</p>
<p>On 13 April 2008, the club announced the dismissal of manager <a href="/wiki/Mirko_Slomka" title="Mirko Slomka">Mirko Slomka</a> after a heavy defeat at the hands of <a href="/wiki/SV_Werder_Bremen" title="SV Werder Bremen">Werder Bremen</a> and elimination from the Champions League. Former players <a href="/wiki/Mike_B%C3%BCskens" title="Mike Büskens">Mike Büskens</a> and <a href="/wiki/Youri_Mulder" title="Youri Mulder">Youri Mulder</a> were put in charge of the first team on an interim basis.</p>
<p>For the <a href="/wiki/2008%E2%80%9309_Bundesliga" title="2008–09 Bundesliga">2008–09 Bundesliga season</a>, Schalke signed a new head coach, <a href="/wiki/Fred_Rutten" title="Fred Rutten">Fred Rutten</a>, previously of <a href="/wiki/FC_Twente" title="FC Twente">Twente</a>. Rutten signed a contract running until June 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> In March 2009, Rutten was sacked and, once more, Mike Büskens, Youri Mulder and Oliver Reck took over the helm.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:142px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Raul_Gonzalez_Blanco_Schalke.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="623" data-file-width="252" height="346" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Raul_Gonzalez_Blanco_Schalke.jpg/140px-Raul_Gonzalez_Blanco_Schalke.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Raul_Gonzalez_Blanco_Schalke.jpg/210px-Raul_Gonzalez_Blanco_Schalke.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f5/Raul_Gonzalez_Blanco_Schalke.jpg 2x" width="140"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Raul_Gonzalez_Blanco_Schalke.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Ra%C3%BAl_(footballer)" title="Raúl (footballer)">Raúl</a>, then all-time top goalscorer in European club competitions, played for Schalke from 2010 to 2012.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 1 July 2009, <a href="/wiki/Felix_Magath" title="Felix Magath">Felix Magath</a>, who had led <a href="/wiki/VfL_Wolfsburg" title="VfL Wolfsburg">VfL Wolfsburg</a> to the top of the table in the Bundesliga, became head coach and general manager of the <i>Königsblauen</i>. The appointment of Magath as manager coincided with a multimillion-euro spending spree, allowing Schalke to acquire internationally-known forwards <a href="/wiki/Klaas-Jan_Huntelaar" title="Klaas-Jan Huntelaar">Klaas-Jan Huntelaar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ra%C3%BAl_(footballer)" title="Raúl (footballer)">Raúl</a>. Magath's tenure at the club was initially successful, seeing the side score a glut of goals in the first few months of the season, though defensive frailties and Magath's questionable squad selection had made him unpopular with Schalke supporters by December 2010. On 16 March 2011, Magath was sacked and replaced with <a href="/wiki/Ralf_Rangnick" title="Ralf Rangnick">Ralf Rangnick</a>, who previously, between 2004 and 2005, had a brief spell being in charge of the team. Within just weeks of his appointment, Rangnick masterminded a 5–2 victory over Inter Milan at the <a href="/wiki/San_Siro" title="San Siro">San Siro</a> during the <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_UEFA_Champions_League_knockout_phase" title="2010–11 UEFA Champions League knockout phase">quarter-finals</a> of the Champions League. Schalke advanced to the <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_UEFA_Champions_League#Semi-finals" title="2010–11 UEFA Champions League">semi-final</a> where they lost 2–0 to <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a> in the first leg and 4–1 in the second leg.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 22 September 2011, Ralf Rangnick announced his immediate resignation as head coach of Schalke 04 due to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Burnout_(psychology)" title="Burnout (psychology)">long-term exhaustion</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> Assistant coach Seppo Eichkorn coached the team as interim manager until the appointment of Huub Stevens on 27 September 2011. Stevens' contract was to run until 30 June 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Schalke04_Barcelona_CL0708_02.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2112" data-file-width="2816" height="225" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Schalke04_Barcelona_CL0708_02.jpg/300px-Schalke04_Barcelona_CL0708_02.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Schalke04_Barcelona_CL0708_02.jpg/450px-Schalke04_Barcelona_CL0708_02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Schalke04_Barcelona_CL0708_02.jpg/600px-Schalke04_Barcelona_CL0708_02.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Schalke04_Barcelona_CL0708_02.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
FC Schalke 04 in the UEFA Champions League line-up against <a href="/wiki/FC_Barcelona" title="FC Barcelona">FC Barcelona</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Despite having legendary status among Schalke supporters, Stevens' return to Schalke was met with some scepticism as fans feared that Stevens, who coached Schalke to the 1997 UEFA Cup win with a rigidly defensive system, could abandon Rangnick's system of attacking play in favour of returning to his 1997 defensive antics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> The doubts of the supporters proved unfounded. Although Schalke played a somewhat inconsistent season, they reached third place in the Bundesliga and therefore direct qualification for the UEFA Champions League.</p>
<p>Schalke had an excellent start to the <a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_Bundesliga" title="2012–13 Bundesliga">2012–13 Bundesliga season</a>, and worked their way to second place in the league by November, just behind Bayern Munich. On 20 October, Schalke traveled to <a href="/wiki/Borussia_Dortmund" title="Borussia Dortmund">Borussia Dortmund</a> for Matchday 8, and were able to defeat the home side 2–1 to secure their first league <a href="/wiki/Revierderby" title="Revierderby">Revierderby</a> win since February 2010 while securing a Champions League place by finishing fourth.</p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2013–14 UEFA Champions League">2013–14 Champions League</a> <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_UEFA_Champions_League_group_stage" title="2013–14 UEFA Champions League group stage">group stage</a>, Schalke's opponents were <a href="/wiki/FC_Steaua_Bucure%C8%99ti" title="FC Steaua București">Steaua București</a>, <a href="/wiki/FC_Basel" title="FC Basel">Basel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C." title="Chelsea F.C.">Chelsea</a>. Schalke ultimately finished the group stage in second place to Chelsea and exited in the round of 16 to <a href="/wiki/Real_Madrid_C.F." title="Real Madrid C.F.">Real Madrid</a>.</p>
<p>The most prominent Schalke addition was the arrival of <a href="/wiki/Kevin-Prince_Boateng" title="Kevin-Prince Boateng">Kevin-Prince Boateng</a> from <a href="/wiki/A.C._Milan" title="A.C. Milan">Milan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Schalke_sign_Kevin_Prince_Boateng_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-Schalke_sign_Kevin_Prince_Boateng-18">[18]</a></sup> After a disappointing first round of the <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_Bundesliga" title="2013–14 Bundesliga">2013–14 Bundesliga</a> that saw Schalke in seventh place in the Bundesliga table, as well as an early exit from the <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_DFB-Pokal" title="2013–14 DFB-Pokal">2013–14 DFB-Pokal</a> in the first knockout round, the club played their most successful second half of the season in club history. The season was marked by a glut of injuries to key squad players, including <a href="/wiki/Jefferson_Farf%C3%A1n" title="Jefferson Farfán">Jefferson Farfán</a> and Klaas-Jan Huntelaar, for almost the entire season. It also led to performance related discussions about head coach Jens Keller. Partially, S04 fielded up to ten young players with potential who played in the S04 youth system throughout the season. Among the brightest S04 young player discoveries of the 2013–14 season were Max Meyer and Leon Goretzka. The young S04 squad won 11 out of 17 games in which S04 retrieved 36 points. At the end of the 2013–14 season, the young S04 squad reached the third place in the league table and thus for the third time in a row qualified for the UEFA Champions League, in which is a feat that S04 have never before achieved.</p>
<p>On 7 October 2014, after a 1–2 defeat to <a href="/wiki/TSG_1899_Hoffenheim" title="TSG 1899 Hoffenheim">1899 Hoffenheim</a> and merely eight points in seven games, Keller was sacked and succeeded by <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Di_Matteo" title="Roberto Di Matteo">Roberto Di Matteo</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-newswirengr.com_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-newswirengr.com-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<div align="center">
<div class="timeline-wrapper"><map id="timeline_b93a09df8d44c52810bbb0203ad2a450" name="timeline_b93a09df8d44c52810bbb0203ad2a450"></map><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/timeline/b93a09df8d44c52810bbb0203ad2a450.png" usemap="#timeline_b93a09df8d44c52810bbb0203ad2a450"/></div>
</div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="12th_richest_in_the_world">12th richest in the world</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Schalke_04&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: 12th richest in the world">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Forbes%27_list_of_the_most_valuable_football_clubs" title="Forbes' list of the most valuable football clubs">Forbes' list of the most valuable football clubs</a></div>

</div>
</div>
<p>The headline sponsors of FC Schalke 04 are the China-based electronics manufacturer <a href="/wiki/Hisense" title="Hisense">Hisense</a> and the Russia-based hydrocarbon giant <a href="/wiki/Gazprom" title="Gazprom">Gazprom</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vladimir_Putin.2C_Gazprom_and_Schalke_04_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-Vladimir_Putin.2C_Gazprom_and_Schalke_04-20">[20]</a></sup> Additional sponsors include the Germany-based insurance group <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ERGO_Insurance_Group" title="ERGO Insurance Group">ERGO Insurance Group</a>; the Germany-based automotive manufacturer <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Group" title="Volkswagen Group">Volkswagen Group</a>; the China-based telecommunications company <a href="/wiki/Huawei" title="Huawei">Huawei</a>; the cyber gambling and sports betting company <a href="/wiki/Bet-at-home.com" title="Bet-at-home.com">bet-at-home.com</a>; the beverage company <a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola" title="Coca-Cola">Coca-Cola</a>; the Germany-based brewery <a href="/wiki/Veltins" title="Veltins">Veltins</a>; and the S04 current squad kit manufacturer Germany-based <a href="/wiki/Adidas" title="Adidas">Adidas</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vladimir_Putin.2C_Gazprom_and_Schalke_04_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-Vladimir_Putin.2C_Gazprom_and_Schalke_04-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>In terms of operating income, Schalke possesses the 7th highest operating income of any football club in the world at €48 million,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Forbes_List_6-2"><a href="#cite_note-Forbes_List-6">[6]</a></sup> and 0% debt as of August 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Schalke_04_-_Forbes_7-3"><a href="#cite_note-Schalke_04_-_Forbes-7">[7]</a></sup> S04 generates the 12th highest revenue of any football club in the world at €198 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Schalke_04_-_Forbes_7-4"><a href="#cite_note-Schalke_04_-_Forbes-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>In May 2014, Schalke 04 were ranked by <a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes Magazine</a> as the <a href="/wiki/Forbes%27_list_of_the_most_valuable_football_clubs" title="Forbes' list of the most valuable football clubs">twelfth richest football club in the world</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Forbes_List_6-3"><a href="#cite_note-Forbes_List-6">[6]</a></sup> at €446 million, an increase of 16% from the previous year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Schalke_04_-_Forbes_7-5"><a href="#cite_note-Schalke_04_-_Forbes-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:left;"></div>

<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/FC_Schalke_04_II" title="FC Schalke 04 II">FC Schalke 04 II</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_former_players">Notable former players</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Schalke_04&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Notable former players">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Grossplastik_Schalke_Koepfe_2001.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="517" data-file-width="629" height="181" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Grossplastik_Schalke_Koepfe_2001.jpg/220px-Grossplastik_Schalke_Koepfe_2001.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Grossplastik_Schalke_Koepfe_2001.jpg/330px-Grossplastik_Schalke_Koepfe_2001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Grossplastik_Schalke_Koepfe_2001.jpg/440px-Grossplastik_Schalke_Koepfe_2001.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>

<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Grossplastik_Schalke_Koepfe_2001.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Stadium">Stadium</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Schalke_04&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Stadium">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tmulti tleft" style="background-color:#0070FF">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:268px;max-width:268px;background-color:#0070FF">
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;background-color:#0070FF;margin:1px;width:132px;max-width:132px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2010-06-03_Arena_AufSchalke_20.jpg"><img alt="Exterior of the Veltins-Arena" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3888" height="87" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/2010-06-03_Arena_AufSchalke_20.jpg/130px-2010-06-03_Arena_AufSchalke_20.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/2010-06-03_Arena_AufSchalke_20.jpg/195px-2010-06-03_Arena_AufSchalke_20.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/2010-06-03_Arena_AufSchalke_20.jpg/260px-2010-06-03_Arena_AufSchalke_20.jpg 2x" width="130"/></a></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;background-color:#0070FF;margin:1px;width:132px;max-width:132px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2010-06-04_Schalke_04-Gesch%C3%A4ftsstelle_01.jpg"><img alt="Training ground of FC Schalke 04 known as the Geschäftsstelle" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3888" height="87" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/2010-06-04_Schalke_04-Gesch%C3%A4ftsstelle_01.jpg/130px-2010-06-04_Schalke_04-Gesch%C3%A4ftsstelle_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/2010-06-04_Schalke_04-Gesch%C3%A4ftsstelle_01.jpg/195px-2010-06-04_Schalke_04-Gesch%C3%A4ftsstelle_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/2010-06-04_Schalke_04-Gesch%C3%A4ftsstelle_01.jpg/260px-2010-06-04_Schalke_04-Gesch%C3%A4ftsstelle_01.jpg 2x" width="130"/></a></div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center;background-color:#FFFFFF"><span style="color:#0070FF">Veltins-Arena exterior and S04 training ground</span></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Schalke's stadium, known as the <a href="/wiki/Veltins-Arena" title="Veltins-Arena">Veltins-Arena</a> under a sponsorship agreement with <a href="/wiki/Veltins" title="Veltins">Veltins</a> brewery, was completed in the summer of 2001 and has a capacity of 62,271 spectators.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stadionkapazit.C3.A4t_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-Stadionkapazit.C3.A4t-1">[1]</a></sup> Schalke regularly draws sell-out crowds to what is widely regarded as one of the most modern and best multi-use facilities in Europe. The facility was previously known as the Arena AufSchalke and replaced the <a href="/wiki/Parkstadion" title="Parkstadion">Parkstadion</a> (capacity of 62,000) built in 1973. Prior to this the club had played its matches in the <a href="/wiki/Gl%C3%BCckauf-Kampfbahn" title="Glückauf-Kampfbahn">Glückauf-Kampfbahn</a> constructed in 1928 with a capacity of 35,000. The facility was used for amateur matches during its latter years with a reduced capacity of just 5,000.</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; width:99%; max-width:808px;">
<div class="thumbinner" style="">
<div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Veltins-Arena_Panorama.jpg" title="An interior design panorama of the S04 Stadium Veltins-Arena"><img alt="" data-file-height="4074" data-file-width="7874" height="414" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Veltins-Arena_Panorama.jpg/800px-Veltins-Arena_Panorama.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Veltins-Arena_Panorama.jpg/1200px-Veltins-Arena_Panorama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Veltins-Arena_Panorama.jpg/1600px-Veltins-Arena_Panorama.jpg 2x" width="800"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="text-align:center">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Veltins-Arena_Panorama.jpg" title="File:Veltins-Arena Panorama.jpg"></a></div>
An <a href="/wiki/Interior_design" title="Interior design">interior design</a> panorama of the S04 Stadium <a href="/wiki/Veltins-Arena" title="Veltins-Arena">Veltins-Arena</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="S04_Ultras_and_Supporters">S04 Ultras and Supporters</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Schalke_04&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: S04 Ultras and Supporters">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Schalke_04_Fans_677.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1900" data-file-width="2500" height="152" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Schalke_04_Fans_677.jpg/200px-Schalke_04_Fans_677.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Schalke_04_Fans_677.jpg/300px-Schalke_04_Fans_677.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Schalke_04_Fans_677.jpg/400px-Schalke_04_Fans_677.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Schalke_04_Fans_677.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
S04 <a href="/wiki/Ultras" title="Ultras">Ultras</a> Gelsenkirchen.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The number of members of Schalke 04 grew from 10,000 in 1991 to 129,672 in 2014. This figure makes Schalke 04 the second-biggest sports club in Germany and third-biggest sports club in the world behind second placed FC Bayern Munich and first placed SL Benfica. FC Schalke 04 has the fourth largest fan-base of any other team in the world. S04 is currently ranked as the 9th best <a href="/wiki/Football_team" title="Football team">football team</a> in <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> and on <a href="/wiki/Continental_Europe" title="Continental Europe">Continental Europe</a> by <a href="/wiki/UEFA" title="UEFA">UEFA</a>'s <a href="/wiki/UEFA_coefficient#UEFA_Team_Ranking" title="UEFA coefficient">UEFA club rankings</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UEFA_Team_Ranking_2015_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-UEFA_Team_Ranking_2015-5">[5]</a></sup> A representation of the Schalke 04 membership structure in 2014 showed, among other things, a female share of 20% and a share of the age group up to 10 years of 14%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mitglied_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mitglied-29">[29]</a></sup> Around 30% of the members were not from North Rhine-Westphalia. Apart from Gelsenkirchen (10,197 members) and its immediate neighboring towns the members of Schalke 04 also come from more distant cities such as Cologne (1117), Berlin (932) and Dortmund (800).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mitglied_29-1"><a href="#cite_note-Mitglied-29">[29]</a></sup> This high growth in Schalke 04 membership is also promoted by promotions of Schalke 04, as from 2013 to further "advertise Schalke 04 brand".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mitglied_29-2"><a href="#cite_note-Mitglied-29">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 21 August 2013, S04 played their first home game, a 2013–14 UEFA Champions League qualifier at the Veltins-Arena against the Greek runners-up (coached by former coach Hub Stevens), drawing 1–1.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Streit_um_einsatz_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-Streit_um_einsatz-31">[31]</a></sup> The match and the result was more than overshadowed by a controversial police operations in the block of the "S04 Ultras Gelsenkirchen" block of the Veltins-Arena against the fans of the away team with nearly 80 injured of the <a href="/wiki/PAOK_FC" title="PAOK FC">PAOK</a> away team's fans injured.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Streit_um_einsatz_31-1"><a href="#cite_note-Streit_um_einsatz-31">[31]</a></sup> The return match was won 3–2 by Schalke without any of their supporters allowed to spectate the match.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Streit_um_einsatz_31-2"><a href="#cite_note-Streit_um_einsatz-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Schalke_04_Fan_Club_Association">Schalke 04 Fan Club Association</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Schalke_04&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Schalke 04 Fan Club Association">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Schalker_Massen01.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="1536" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Schalker_Massen01.jpg/300px-Schalker_Massen01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Schalker_Massen01.jpg/450px-Schalker_Massen01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Schalker_Massen01.jpg/600px-Schalker_Massen01.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Schalker_Massen01.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
S04 <a href="/wiki/Ultras" title="Ultras">Ultras</a> Gelsenkirchen with an alliance of S04 supporters patrolling the streets of Gelsenkirchen on matchday for away team fans insight.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Schalke 04 Fan Club Association (SFCV) as an umbrella organization, according to his own statement has an estimated 1500 fan clubs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> Of the listed by the SFCV, 860 S04 fan clubs (October 2012) in which an estimated 200 were in Ruhr, 360 in the rest of North Rhine-Westphalia, and 300 in the other federal states.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> A member of the board of SFCV has a permanent seat on the board of FC Schalke 04 and in 2013 SFCV merged with the "Ultras Gelsenkirchen" and later the supporters' club, Schalke Fan-Initiative eV with several members of strong fan groups from the SFCV, as is clear from the merger of the SFCV with the fan section of S04 has not adequately represented the fan interests.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Friendships">Friendships</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Schalke_04&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Friendships">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The fan-base of Schalke is friendly connected with the supporters of the <a href="/wiki/1._FC_N%C3%BCrnberg" title="1. FC Nürnberg">1. FC Nürnberg</a> and the Dutch club <a href="/wiki/FC_Twente" title="FC Twente">FC Twente</a>. The friendship with Nürnberg is the oldest connection between two fan-bases in Germany. Before a match between both clubs, the official club songs are played.</p>
<p>The Ultras have also a friendship with the supporters of the Macedonian club <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vardar_Skopje" title="Vardar Skopje">Vardar Skopje</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Club_songs">Club songs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Schalke_04&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Club songs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><i>Blau und weiß, wie lieb ich Dich</i> ("Blue and White, How I Love You") is the official club song.</li>
<li><i>Das Steigerlied</i>, traditional German mining song, play before every match.</li>
<li><i>Blau und Weiß ein Leben lang</i> ("Blue and white a life-long") is the goal tune.</li>
<li><i>Königsblauer S04</i> ("Royal Blue S04") played after every match</li>
</ul>
<p>Popular unofficial <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Football_chants" title="Football chants">chants</a> are</p>
<ul>
<li><i>Der Mythos vom Schalker Markt</i> ("The Myth of the Schalke Market"),</li>
<li><i>Opa Pritschikowski</i> ("Grandpa Pritschikowski"),</li>
<li><i>Von der Emscher bis zum Bosporus</i> ("From the Emscher to the Bosphorus"),</li>
<li><i>Wir schlugen Roda...</i> ("We beat Roda..."),</li>
<li><i>Die Eurofighter sind wieder da</i> ("The Eurofighter are back again"),</li>
<li><i>Für deine Farben leben und sterben wir</i> ("For your colours we live and die"),</li>
<li><i>Wir lieben alle nur den FC Schalke</i> ("We all love only FC Schalke"),</li>
<li><i>Wir sind die Fans</i> ("We are the fans"),</li>
<li><i>Hurra wir sind die Schalker Knappen</i> ("Hurray we are the Schalke <a href="/wiki/Miner" title="Miner">Knappen</a>"),</li>
<li><i>Kohle unter unser'n Füßen</i> ("Coal under our feet"), and</li>
<li><i>Steht auf, wenn ihr Schalker seid</i> ("Stand up if you're Schalke"), sung to the melody of "<a href="/wiki/Go_West_(song)" title="Go West (song)">Go West</a>" by the <a href="/wiki/Pet_Shop_Boys" title="Pet Shop Boys">Pet Shop Boys</a> (itself a cover of a <a href="/wiki/Village_People" title="Village People">Village People</a> song).</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Revierderby">Revierderby</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Schalke_04&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Revierderby">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Revierderby" title="Revierderby">Revierderby</a></div>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; width:99%; max-width:808px;">

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_popular_culture">In popular culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Schalke_04&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: In popular culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2010-06-03_Arena_AufSchalke_07.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3888" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/2010-06-03_Arena_AufSchalke_07.jpg/220px-2010-06-03_Arena_AufSchalke_07.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/2010-06-03_Arena_AufSchalke_07.jpg/330px-2010-06-03_Arena_AufSchalke_07.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/2010-06-03_Arena_AufSchalke_07.jpg/440px-2010-06-03_Arena_AufSchalke_07.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2010-06-03_Arena_AufSchalke_07.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Cleat_(shoe)" title="Cleat (shoe)">cleats</a> worn by the entire S04 squad players in the 1920s displayed at the museum of FC Schalke 04.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Schalke has been subject of a feature-length film called <i><a href="/wiki/Fu%C3%9Fball_ist_unser_Leben" title="Fußball ist unser Leben">Fußball ist unser Leben</a></i> ("Football is our life"), shown in 1999. Actors <a href="/wiki/Uwe_Ochsenknecht" title="Uwe Ochsenknecht">Uwe Ochsenknecht</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ralf_Richter_(actor)" title="Ralf Richter (actor)">Ralf Richter</a>, both of whom were in the award-winning film <i><a href="/wiki/Das_Boot" title="Das Boot">Das Boot</a></i> played the main roles, while many persons associated with Schalke had cameo roles, such as manager <a href="/wiki/Rudi_Assauer" title="Rudi Assauer">Rudi Assauer</a>, coaches <a href="/wiki/Huub_Stevens" title="Huub Stevens">Huub Stevens</a> and Helmut Schulte, and player Yves Eigenrauch. Also featured were prominent fans like Manfred Breuckmann, Ulrich Potofski or DJ Hooligan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sp_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-sp-36">[36]</a></sup> The film is a comedy about "Hans", a Schalke fanatic, and his three pals who somehow get involved in kidnapping and trying to bring back to form the team's new star player "Di Ospeo" and in the process bet Hans' house that their idol will score in the final game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sp_36-1"><a href="#cite_note-sp-36">[36]</a></sup> Some critics considered <i>Football is our life</i> to be "one of the worst German comedies ever."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sp_36-2"><a href="#cite_note-sp-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<p>"Schalke" is mentioned in the film <i>Das Boot</i> when the <a href="/wiki/Boatswain" title="Boatswain">bosun</a> tells the crew in their ward room, "I got bad news for you men. Schalke lost 5–0, looks like we won't be in the final this year."</p>
<div style="clear:left;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Honours">Honours</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Schalke_04&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Honours">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Domestic">Domestic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Schalke_04&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Domestic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:387px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Meisterschale_Schalke-Museum.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="2592" height="385" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Meisterschale_Schalke-Museum.jpg/385px-Meisterschale_Schalke-Museum.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Meisterschale_Schalke-Museum.jpg/578px-Meisterschale_Schalke-Museum.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Meisterschale_Schalke-Museum.jpg/770px-Meisterschale_Schalke-Museum.jpg 2x" width="385"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Meisterschale_Schalke-Museum.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Schalke 04 have captured the <a href="/wiki/List_of_German_football_champions" title="List of German football champions">German championship</a> 7 times</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><b><a href="/wiki/Bundesliga" title="Bundesliga">Bundesliga</a>/<a href="/wiki/List_of_German_football_champions" title="List of German football champions">German Championship</a></b></p>
<ul>
<li><b>Winners (7):</b> <a href="/wiki/1934_German_football_championship" title="1934 German football championship">1934</a>, <a href="/wiki/1935_German_football_championship" title="1935 German football championship">1935</a>, <a href="/wiki/1937_German_football_championship" title="1937 German football championship">1937</a>, <a href="/wiki/1939_German_football_championship" title="1939 German football championship">1939</a>, <a href="/wiki/1940_German_football_championship" title="1940 German football championship">1940</a>, <a href="/wiki/1942_German_football_championship" title="1942 German football championship">1942</a>, <a href="/wiki/1958_German_football_championship" title="1958 German football championship">1958</a>
<ul>
<li><b>Runners-up (9):</b> <a href="/wiki/1933_German_football_championship" title="1933 German football championship">1933</a>, <a href="/wiki/1938_German_football_championship" title="1938 German football championship">1938</a>, <a href="/wiki/1941_German_football_championship" title="1941 German football championship">1941</a>, <a href="/wiki/1971%E2%80%9372_Bundesliga" title="1971–72 Bundesliga">1971–72</a>, <a href="/wiki/1976%E2%80%9377_Bundesliga" title="1976–77 Bundesliga">1976–77</a>, <a href="/wiki/2000%E2%80%9301_Bundesliga" title="2000–01 Bundesliga">2000–01</a>, <a href="/wiki/2004%E2%80%9305_Bundesliga" title="2004–05 Bundesliga">2004–05</a>, <a href="/wiki/2006%E2%80%9307_Bundesliga" title="2006–07 Bundesliga">2006–07</a>, <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_Bundesliga" title="2009–10 Bundesliga">2009–10</a></li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<p><b><a href="/wiki/DFB-Pokal" title="DFB-Pokal">DFB-Pokal/German Cup</a></b></p>
<ul>
<li><b>Winners (5):</b> <a href="/wiki/1937_Tschammerpokal" title="1937 Tschammerpokal">1937</a>, <a href="/wiki/1971%E2%80%9372_DFB-Pokal" title="1971–72 DFB-Pokal">1971–72</a>, <a href="/wiki/2000%E2%80%9301_DFB-Pokal" title="2000–01 DFB-Pokal">2000–01</a>, <a href="/wiki/2001%E2%80%9302_DFB-Pokal" title="2001–02 DFB-Pokal">2001–02</a>, <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_DFB-Pokal" title="2010–11 DFB-Pokal">2010–11</a>
<ul>
<li><b>Runners-up (7):</b> <a href="/wiki/1935_Tschammerpokal" title="1935 Tschammerpokal">1935</a>, <a href="/wiki/1936_Tschammerpokal" title="1936 Tschammerpokal">1936</a>, <a href="/wiki/1941_Tschammerpokal" title="1941 Tschammerpokal">1941</a>, <a href="/wiki/1942_Tschammerpokal" title="1942 Tschammerpokal">1942</a>, <a href="/wiki/1954%E2%80%9355_DFB-Pokal" title="1954–55 DFB-Pokal">1954–55</a>, <a href="/wiki/1968%E2%80%9369_DFB-Pokal" title="1968–69 DFB-Pokal">1968–69</a>, <a href="/wiki/2004%E2%80%9305_DFB-Pokal" title="2004–05 DFB-Pokal">2004–05</a></li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>

<ul>
<li><b>Runners-up:</b> <a href="/wiki/2001_DFB-Ligapokal" title="2001 DFB-Ligapokal">2001</a>, <a href="/wiki/2002_DFB-Ligapokal" title="2002 DFB-Ligapokal">2002</a>, <a href="/wiki/2007_DFL-Ligapokal" title="2007 DFL-Ligapokal">2007</a></li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>

<ul>

</ul>
</li>
</ul>

<ul>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_managers">Notable managers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Schalke_04&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Notable managers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bas_van_Veenendaal.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="600" height="267" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Bas_van_Veenendaal.JPG/200px-Bas_van_Veenendaal.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Bas_van_Veenendaal.JPG/300px-Bas_van_Veenendaal.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Bas_van_Veenendaal.JPG/400px-Bas_van_Veenendaal.JPG 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bas_van_Veenendaal.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Huub Stevens managed the club in two spells: firstly, from 1996 to 2002, where he won the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Europa_League" title="Europa League">UEFA Cup</a> in <a href="/wiki/1997_UEFA_Cup_Final" title="1997 UEFA Cup Final">1997</a>, and secondly, from 2011 to 2012. He was voted 'Coach of the Century' by Schalke fans in 1999.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">For more details on this topic, see <a href="/wiki/List_of_FC_Schalke_04_managers" title="List of FC Schalke 04 managers">List of FC Schalke 04 managers</a>.</div>
