<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="S04_other_departments">S04 other departments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Schalke_04&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: S04 other departments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Women.27s_football">Women's football</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Schalke_04&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Women's football">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_association_football" title="Women's association football">women's football</a>, FC Schalke 04 have achieved some notable successes in the late seventies and early eighties of the 20th century. The S04 women's team was five times Westphalia champion and twice cup winners as well as competing in the German Championship and in the DFB Cup ended up being each in the first round. Mid-nineteen eighties, the S04 women's team was dissolved. Since the 2007–08 season, S04 is cooperating with the women footballers of the second division 1 FFC Recklinghausen.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Basketball">Basketball</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Schalke_04&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Basketball">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a> department of FC Schalke 04 played in the 1988–89 season in the National Basketball League <a href="/wiki/Basketball_Bundesliga" title="Basketball Bundesliga">Basketball Bundesliga</a> and from 2004 for several seasons in the <a href="/wiki/2._Basketball_Bundesliga" title="2. Basketball Bundesliga">ProA</a>, the second highest basketball league in Germany.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> 2009 saw the Schalke 04 voluntary withdrawal of Schalke 04 from the ProA. Currently, the Schalke 04 basketball department competes in the 1 Regionalliga West.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Blind_soccer">Blind soccer</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Schalke_04&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Blind soccer">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>This departement was founded in 2015. The squad plays in the National Blind Soccer League (Blindenfußball-Bundesliga).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Handball">Handball</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Schalke_04&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Handball">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Team_handball" title="Team handball">handball</a> department of FC Schalke 04 was founded in 1926. In 1929 it competed in the Gaumeister prior to competing in the <a href="/wiki/Gauliga" title="Gauliga">Gauliga</a> until the end of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Third_Reich" title="Third Reich">Third Reich</a>, the then top division. After the Second World War, except for a few years in the league, the S04 handball department did not build on the successes. Currently the S04 handball department competes in the national league.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Athletics">Athletics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Schalke_04&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Athletics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Athletics_(track_and_field)" title="Athletics (track and field)">athletics (track and field)</a> department of FC Schalke 04 was founded in 1922. Famous members were multiple German champion in <a href="/wiki/Sprint_(running)" title="Sprint (running)">sprint</a> such as Erika Rost; and the winner of the silver medal in the <a href="/wiki/Decathlon" title="Decathlon">decathlon</a> at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1996_Olympic_Games" title="1996 Olympic Games">1996 Olympic Games</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frank_Busemann" title="Frank Busemann">Frank Busemann</a>; and the <a href="/wiki/2003_European_Athletics_Junior_Championships" title="2003 European Athletics Junior Championships">2003 European Athletics Junior Championships</a> gold in <a href="/wiki/200_metres" title="200 metres">200 metres</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sebastian_Ernst" title="Sebastian Ernst">Sebastian Ernst</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Table_tennis">Table tennis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Schalke_04&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Table tennis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Table_tennis" title="Table tennis">table tennis</a> department of FC Schalke 04 was founded in 1947. In the 1952–53 season, the FC Schalke 04 table tennis department competed for a year in the big leagues, up unto the foundation of the <a href="/wiki/Bundesliga_(table_tennis)" title="Bundesliga (table tennis)">table tennis Bundesliga</a> in 1966, the top division in Germany. In the 2013–14 season S04 table tennis department competed in the Westphalia district league. The FC Schalke 04 table tennis department women's team was one of the early participants in the 1950s in the national league, until it was withdrawn in 1956.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="eSports">eSports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Schalke_04&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: eSports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/FC_Schalke_04_League_of_Legends" title="FC Schalke 04 League of Legends">FC Schalke 04 League of Legends</a></div>
<p>In 2016, Schalke opened an eSports department and acquired <i><a href="/wiki/League_of_Legends" title="League of Legends">League of Legends</a></i> team <a href="/wiki/Elements_(League_of_Legends)" title="Elements (League of Legends)">Elements</a>, becoming the second professional sports team with a <i>LoL</i> division after <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Besiktas_Jimnastik_Kulubu" title="Besiktas Jimnastik Kulubu">Besiktas</a> acquired the roster of Turkish team Aces High the previous year. In early June, they debuted in the European <a href="/wiki/League_of_Legends_Championship_Series" title="League of Legends Championship Series"><i>League of Legends</i> Championship Series</a>, officially organized by developer <a href="/wiki/Riot_Games" title="Riot Games">Riot Games</a> and the top level of professional <i>League of Legends</i> competition in Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> The club also announced former <a href="/wiki/Rot-Wei%C3%9F_Oberhausen" title="Rot-Weiß Oberhausen">Rot-Weiß Oberhausen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sportfreunde_Siegen" title="Sportfreunde Siegen">Sportfreunde Siegen</a> midfielder and <a href="/wiki/SK_Gaming" title="SK Gaming">SK Gaming</a> co-founder <a href="/wiki/Tim_Reichert" title="Tim Reichert">Tim Reichert</a> as Head of ESport.</p>

<li>Bodo Berg: <i>More than a game: from the life of a football fan; with photos of Yves own smoke</i>. Verlg the workshop, Göttingen 2000, <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/3895332992">ISBN 3-89533-299-2</a>.</li>

<li>Stefan Goch / Norbert Silver Bach: <i>Between blue and white is gray</i>, Essen 2005, <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/3898614336">ISBN 3-89861-433-6</a>.</li>
<li>Hardy Green: <i>Faith, Love, Schalke. The complete history of FC Schalke 04</i>, The Workshop, Göttingen 2011, <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9783895337475">ISBN 978-3-89533-747-5</a>.</li>
<li>Helmut Wood: <i>Schalke is priceless</i>, Gelsenkirchen, 1991, <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/3924984301">ISBN 3-924984-30-1</a> .</li>
<li>Helmut Wood: <i>Schalke smile. Curiosities and concrete of fans and dreamers – experienced and collected</i>, Gelsenkirchen 1984, <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/3980076466">ISBN 3-9800764-6-6</a>.</li>
<li>William Herbert Koch: <i>The Royal Blues: the phenomenon Schalke 04</i>, Düsseldorf 1973, <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/3770003659">ISBN 3-7700-0365-9</a>.</li>
<li>Olivier Kruschinski: <i>Blue and white for a lifetime. A season with Schalke</i>, Herten 2005, <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/3938152044">ISBN 3-938152-04-4</a>.</li>
<li>Georg Röwekamp: <i>The legend lives on. The history of FC Schalke 04</i>, Göttingen 1996 [and newer edition], <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/3895331643">ISBN 3-89533-164-3</a>.</li>
<li>Schalke Fan Initiative (Eds.), <i>The tip of the Eichbergs. Most scandals of FC Schalke 04</i>. plain text, Essen 2005, <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/3898613933">ISBN 3-89861-393-3</a>.</li>
<li>Jörg Seven Eick, Thomas Spiegel, Gerd Voss (Eds.): <i>100 Schalke years – 100 stories Schalke</i>. Plain text, Essen 2004, <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/3898613216">ISBN 3-89861-321-6</a>.</li>
